Source Code

These source-code files were transcribed from a printout in Don Eyles's personal collection, scanned by archive.org, and financially sponsored by Linden Sims. A team of volunteers performed the transcription and proof-reading. The scanned page images are available at the Virtual AGC Project website, as well as higher-quality (but much larger) images at the Virtual AGC Project's collection in the Internet Archive. Report any problems by creating "issues" at the Virtual AGC Project's GitHub Repository.

Notations on the program listing read, in part:

	GAP:  ASSEMBLE REVISION 56 OF AGC PROGRAM ZERLINA BY ZOROASTER
	9:12 OCT. 21,1970
Note that the date is the date of the printout, not the date of the program revision. 

000002,000002:                                                                                                  #  Copyright:    Public domain.
000003,000003:                                                                                                  #  Filename:     MAIN.agc
000004,000004:                                                                                                  #  Purpose:      The main source file for Zerlina 56, the final revision of
000005,000005:                                                                                                  #                Don Eyles's offline development program for the variable 
000006,000006:                                                                                                  #                guidance period servicer. It also includes a new P66 with LPD 
000007,000007:                                                                                                  #                (Landing Point Designator) capability, based on an idea of John 
000008,000008:                                                                                                  #                Young's. Neither of these advanced features were actually flown,
000009,000009:                                                                                                  #                but Zerlina was also the birthplace of other big improvements to
000010,000010:                                                                                                  #                Luminary including the terrain model and new (Luminary 1E)
000011,000011:                                                                                                  #                analog display programs. Zerlina was branched off of Luminary 145,
000012,000012:                                                                                                  #                and revision 56 includes all changes up to and including Luminary
000013,000013:                                                                                                  #                183. It is therefore quite close to the Apollo 14 program,
000014,000014:                                                                                                  #                Luminary 178, where not modified with new features.
000015,000015:                                                                                                  #  Assembler:    yaYUL
000016,000016:                                                                                                  #  Contact:      Ron Burkey <info@sandroid.org>.
000017,000017:                                                                                                  #  Website:      www.ibiblio.org/apollo/index.html
000018,000018:                                                                                                  #  Mod history:  2017-07-28 MAS  Created.
000019,000019: 
000020,000020:                                                                                                  #  MAIN.agc is a little different from the other Zerlina 56 AGC source-code files, 
000021,000021:                                                                                                  #  in that it doesn't represent anything that appears directly in the original source.  
000022,000022:                                                                                                  #  For organizational purposes, the huge monolithic source code has been split
000023,000023:                                                                                                  #  into smaller, more manageable chunks--i.e., into individual source 
000024,000024:                                                                                                  #  files.  Those files are rejoined within this file as "includes".  It just makes
000025,000025:                                                                                                  #  it a little easier to work with.  The code chunks correspond to natural divisions
000026,000026:                                                                                                  #  into sub-programs.  In fact, these divisions are more-or-less specified by
000027,000027:                                                                                                  #  the source code itself.  Refer to the ASSEMBLY_AND_OPERATION_INFORMATION.agc
000028,000028:                                                                                                  #  file's TABLE OF LOG CARDS.
000029,000029:
